A Tornado WSO of <a href="/wiki/No._12_Squadron_RAF" title="No. 12 Squadron RAF">No. 12 Squadron</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:RAF_Regiment_Gunner.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/RAF_Regiment_Gunner.jpg/220px-RAF_Regiment_Gunner.jpg" width="220" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/RAF_Regiment_Gunner.jpg/330px-RAF_Regiment_Gunner.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/RAF_Regiment_Gunner.jpg/440px-RAF_Regiment_Gunner.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4800" data-file-height="3360" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:RAF_Regiment_Gunner.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An <a href="/wiki/RAF_Regiment" title="RAF Regiment">RAF Regiment</a> Gunner</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li>RAF <a href="/wiki/Aviator" class="mw-redirect" title="Aviator">pilots</a> and weapon systems officers (WSO) (formerly known as <a href="/wiki/Flight_officer" title="Flight officer">navigators</a>) are commissioned officers of the Flying Branch. i.e., Fg(P) or Fg(WSO). Formerly in the General Duties branch, which is now reserved for wing commanders and above from any previous branch.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup></li>
<li>Non-commissioned (NCO) aircrew known as weapon systems operators (WSOp), fulfil the specialist roles of air engineer (E), air electronics operator (AEOp), air loadmaster (ALM) and air signaller (S). Though they are now known collectively as weapon systems operators, individual trade specialisations remain. Commissioned officer specialists are promoted from within branch to become Fg(WSO).<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>The majority of the members of the RAF serve in support roles on the ground:</p>
<ul>
<li>Aerospace Battle Managers(Officers), Aerospace Systems Managers/Operators(Other Ranks) (formally Fighter Controllers(FC)) control RAF and NATO aircraft. The FC control the interception of enemy aircraft while the ATC provide air traffic services at RAF stations and to the majority of en-route military aircraft in UK airspace.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[50]</a></sup></li>
<li>RAF Flight Operations Officers are involved with the planning and co-ordination of all Flying Operations. Flight Operations Officers can be found in every RAF Flying Station and Squadron.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[51]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/RAF_Intelligence" title="RAF Intelligence">RAF Intelligence</a> Officers and Intelligence Analysts support all operational activities by providing timely and accurate indicators and warnings. They conduct detailed all source <a href="/wiki/Military_intelligence" title="Military intelligence">military intelligence</a> fusion and analysis by utilising classified and open source information including imagery, human and communications (signals) intelligence. Intelligence is used to inform commanders of the assessed capabilities and intentions of the enemy for strategic / operational planning and targeting. They also tailor the information to brief aircrews for mission planning and other tactical units (such as RAF Regiment) for Force Protection.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/RAF_Regiment" title="RAF Regiment">RAF Regiment</a> is the RAF's <a href="/wiki/Infantry" title="Infantry">infantry</a> unit, its officers and gunners defend RAF airfields from attack.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup> The RAF Regiment is also responsible for <a href="/wiki/CBRN" class="mw-redirect" title="CBRN">CBRN</a> defence<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[54]</a></sup> and training the rest of the RAF in ground defence.</li>
<li>RAF Police are the <a href="/wiki/Military_police" title="Military police">military police</a> of the RAF.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[55]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Engineering_Officer" class="mw-redirect" title="Engineering Officer">Engineering Officers</a> and technicians are employed to maintain and repair the equipment used by the RAF. This includes routine preparation for flight and maintenance on aircraft, arming aircraft with weapons, as well as deeper level repair work on aircraft systems, IT systems, ground based radar, vehicles, ground support equipment, etc.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[56]</a></sup></li>
<li>Flight Operations Officers assist in the planning, tasking, co-ordination and monitoring of air operations.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[57]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Logistics_Officer" title="Logistics Officer">Logistics Officers</a> manage the movement of the people, transport and equipment necessary to keep aircraft flying. They are the custodians of the supply chain; responsible for catering within the UK, and on exercises and operations overseas; purchase and store equipment/fuel and operate IT systems that manage RAF Logistics.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[58]</a></sup></li>
<li>Personnel Branch officers (Support and Training specialisations) and associated trades (Personnel Support and Physical Training Instructor) are involved with human resources management, training management, physical education, parachute instruction, media handling, infrastructure management, accounts, administration of Service law, personnel and recruitment.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[59]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/RAF_Medical_Branch" class="mw-redirect" title="RAF Medical Branch">RAF Medical Branch</a> provides healthcare at home and on deployed operations, including aeromedical evacuation services. Medical officers are the doctors of the RAF and have specialist expertise in aviation medicine to support aircrew and their protective equipment. Medical officers can go on aeromedical evacuations, providing vital assistance on search-and-rescue missions or emergency relief flights worldwide. RAF Medical Officers are either based in primary care on operations or on RAF stations in the UK or in one of six Ministry of Defence Hospital Units (MDHU's) around the UK as specialist practitioners.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force_Chaplains_Branch" title="Royal Air Force Chaplains Branch">RAF Chaplains Branch</a> provides spiritual and moral support for RAF personnel and their families.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[61]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/RAF_Legal_Branch" title="RAF Legal Branch">RAF Legal Branch</a> provides legal advice on discipline / criminal law and operations law.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[62]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Specialist_training_and_education">Specialist training and education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Air_Force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Specialist training and education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Royal Air Force operates several units and centres for the provision of non-generic training and education. These include the Royal Air Force Leadership Centre and the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force_Centre_for_Air_Power_Studies" title="Royal Air Force Centre for Air Power Studies">Royal Air Force Centre for Air Power Studies</a>, both based at RAF Cranwell, and the <a href="/wiki/Air_Warfare_Centre" title="Air Warfare Centre">Air Warfare Centre</a>, based at RAF Waddington and <a href="/wiki/RAF_Cranwell" title="RAF Cranwell">RAF Cranwell</a>. NCO training and developmental courses occur at <a href="/wiki/RAF_Halton" title="RAF Halton">RAF Halton</a> and officer courses occur at the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Services_Command_and_Staff_College" title="Joint Services Command and Staff College">Joint Services Command and Staff College</a> at Shrivenham.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Aircraft">Aircraft</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Air_Force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Aircraft">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_aircraft_of_the_RAF" class="mw-redirect" title="List of aircraft of the RAF">List of aircraft of the RAF</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_active_United_Kingdom_military_aircraft" title="List of active United Kingdom military aircraft">List of active United Kingdom military aircraft</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/British_military_aircraft_designation_systems" title="British military aircraft designation systems">British military aircraft designations</a> generally comprise a <i>type name</i> followed by a <i><a href="/wiki/Mark_(designation)" title="Mark (designation)">mark number</a></i> which includes an alphabetical <i>rôle prefix</i>. For example, the <i>Typhoon F2</i> was designated as a fighter by the 'F', and the second variant of the type to be produced.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Combat_Air">Combat Air</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Air_Force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Combat Air">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <b><a href="/wiki/Eurofighter_Typhoon_FGR4" class="mw-redirect" title="Eurofighter Typhoon FGR4">Eurofighter Typhoon FGR4</a></b> is the RAF's only air defence fighter aircraft, with a total of six squadrons based across <a href="/wiki/RAF_Coningsby" title="RAF Coningsby">RAF Coningsby</a> and <a href="/wiki/RAF_Lossiemouth" title="RAF Lossiemouth">RAF Lossiemouth</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-RAFTYPH_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RAFTYPH-64">[63]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[64]</a></sup> following the retirement of the <a href="/wiki/Panavia_Tornado_ADV" title="Panavia Tornado ADV">Panavia Tornado F3</a> in late March 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-Retirement_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Retirement-66">[65]</a></sup> Their task is to defend UK airspace. In October 2007 it was announced that <a href="/wiki/MoD_Boscombe_Down" title="MoD Boscombe Down">MoD Boscombe Down</a>, <a href="/wiki/RNAS_Culdrose_(HMS_Seahawk)" title="RNAS Culdrose (HMS Seahawk)">RNAS Culdrose</a> and <a href="/wiki/RAF_Marham" title="RAF Marham">RAF Marham</a> would also be used as <a href="/wiki/Quick_Reaction_Alert" title="Quick Reaction Alert">Quick Reaction Alert</a> bases from early 2008, offering around-the-clock fighter coverage for the South and South West of UK airspace when a direct threat has been identified.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>The RAF has five front-line and one reserve Typhoon units; <a href="/wiki/No._3_Squadron_RAF" title="No. 3 Squadron RAF">3 (Fighter) Squadron</a>, <a href="/wiki/No._11_Squadron_RAF" title="No. 11 Squadron RAF">XI Squadron</a> and <a href="/wiki/No._29_Squadron_RAF" title="No. 29 Squadron RAF">29 (Reserve) Squadron</a> (<a href="/wiki/Operational_Conversion_Unit" class="mw-redirect" title="Operational Conversion Unit">Operational Conversion Unit</a>) based at <a href="/wiki/RAF_Coningsby" title="RAF Coningsby">RAF Coningsby</a>, with <a href="/wiki/1_Squadron_RAF" class="mw-redirect" title="1 Squadron RAF">1 (Fighter) Squadron</a>, <a href="/wiki/No._2_Squadron_RAF" title="No. 2 Squadron RAF">II (Army Cooperation) Squadron</a> and <a href="/wiki/No._6_Squadron_RAF" title="No. 6 Squadron RAF">6 Squadron</a> based at <a href="/wiki/RAF_Lossiemouth" title="RAF Lossiemouth">RAF Lossiemouth</a>. On 23 November 2015 it was announced that two additional front-line Typhoon squadrons will be formed consisting of Tranche 1 versions.<sup id="cite_ref-RAFTYPH_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RAFTYPH-64">[63]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>The mainstay of the strike fleet are the squadrons of <b><a href="/wiki/Panavia_Tornado" title="Panavia Tornado">Tornado GR4s</a></b>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup> These supersonic aircraft can carry a wide range of weaponry, including <a href="/wiki/Storm_Shadow" title="Storm Shadow">Storm Shadow</a> cruise missiles, laser-guided bombs and the <a href="/wiki/ASRAAM" title="ASRAAM">ASRAAM missile</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup> Since June 2008, the <a href="/wiki/Eurofighter_Typhoon_variants#Typhoon_FGR4" title="Eurofighter Typhoon variants">Eurofighter Typhoon FGR4</a> has also been capable of being deployed operationally in the air-to-ground role.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup> The RAF has three operational Tornado units, with <sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[71]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/No._9_Squadron_RAF" title="No. 9 Squadron RAF">IX (Bomber) Squadron</a>, <a href="/wiki/No._12_Squadron_RAF" title="No. 12 Squadron RAF">12 (Bomber) Squadron</a> and <a href="/wiki/No._31_Squadron_RAF" title="No. 31 Squadron RAF">31 Squadron</a> based at <a href="/wiki/RAF_Marham" title="RAF Marham">RAF Marham</a>. With the aircraft type nearing its retirement and replacement by the F-35, the <a href="/wiki/RAF_Lossiemouth" title="RAF Lossiemouth">RAF Lossiemouth</a>-based <a href="/wiki/No._15_Squadron_RAF" title="No. 15 Squadron RAF">15 (Reserve) Squadron</a> (the Tornado Operational Conversion Unit)<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup> was disbanded in March 2017.</p>
<p>The Tornado was previously supplemented by the <a href="/wiki/BAE_Harrier_II" class="mw-redirect" title="BAE Harrier II">Harrier GR7/GR9</a> in the strike and <a href="/wiki/Close_air_support" title="Close air support">close air support</a> roles, and to counter enemy air defences. The Harrier fleet was withdrawn in December 2010 following the <a href="/wiki/Strategic_Defence_and_Security_Review_2010" title="Strategic Defence and Security Review 2010">Strategic Defence and Security Review</a>; the Tornado GR4 is due to retire in March 2019 and be replaced by the <a href="/wiki/Eurofighter_Typhoon" title="Eurofighter Typhoon">Eurofighter Typhoon</a> and <b><a href="/wiki/F-35_Lightning_II" class="mw-redirect" title="F-35 Lightning II">F-35 Lightning&#160;II</a></b>. On 23 November 2015 it was announced that a total of 138 F-35Bs will be ordered.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup></p>
<center>

<h3><span id="Intelligence,_Surveillance,_Target_Acquisition,_and_Reconnaissance_(ISTAR)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Intelligence.2C_Surveillance.2C_Target_Acquisition.2C_and_Reconnaissance_.28ISTAR.29"><a href="/wiki/Intelligence,_surveillance,_target_acquisition,_and_reconnaissance" title="Intelligence, surveillance, target acquisition, and reconnaissance">Intelligence, Surveillance, Target Acquisition, and Reconnaissance</a> (ISTAR)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Air_Force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Intelligence, Surveillance, Target Acquisition, and Reconnaissance (ISTAR)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <b><a href="/wiki/Boeing_E-3_Sentry" title="Boeing E-3 Sentry">Sentry AEW1</a></b>, based at <a href="/wiki/RAF_Waddington" title="RAF Waddington">RAF Waddington</a>, provides airborne early warning to detect incoming enemy aircraft and to co-ordinate the aerial battlefield.</p>
<p>The <b><a href="/wiki/Raytheon_Sentinel" title="Raytheon Sentinel">Sentinel R1</a></b> (also known as ASTOR – Airborne STand-Off Radar) provides a ground radar-surveillance platform based on the Bombardier Global Express long range business jet. These were supplemented in 2009 by four ( a fifth was added later) <b><a href="/wiki/Beechcraft_Super_King_Air" title="Beechcraft Super King Air">Beechcraft Shadow R1</a></b> aircraft equipped for the <a href="/wiki/ISTAR" class="mw-redirect" title="ISTAR">ISTAR</a> role over Afghanistan.<sup id="cite_ref-shadow_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shadow-77">[76]</a></sup> Three more Shadow aircraft will be procured as per the 2015 Defence Review. The Tornado GR4A is fitted with cameras and sensors in the visual, infra-red and radar ranges of the spectrum.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ten <b><a href="/wiki/General_Atomics_MQ-9_Reaper" title="General Atomics MQ-9 Reaper">MQ-9 Reaper</a></b> Unmanned aerial vehicles have been purchased to support operations in Iraq and <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>. They are operated by <a href="/wiki/No._39_Squadron_RAF" title="No. 39 Squadron RAF">No. 39 Squadron RAF</a> based at <a href="/wiki/Creech_Air_Force_Base" title="Creech Air Force Base">Creech Air Force Base</a> and <a href="/wiki/No._13_Squadron_RAF" title="No. 13 Squadron RAF">13 Squadron</a> at <a href="/wiki/RAF_Waddington" title="RAF Waddington">RAF Waddington</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[78]</a></sup> Three <b><a href="/wiki/Boeing_RC-135" title="Boeing RC-135">Boeing RC-135W Rivet Joint</a></b> replaced the Nimrod R1 fleet in the <a href="/wiki/Signals_intelligence" title="Signals intelligence">signals intelligence</a> role. The Nimrod fleet was retired in 2011, and the RAF will share signals aircraft of the US Air Force until the three RC-135s enter service between 2014 and 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup> The aircraft will be <a href="/wiki/Boeing_KC-135_Stratotanker" title="Boeing KC-135 Stratotanker">Boeing KC-135 Stratotanker</a> tankers converted to RC-135W standard in the most complex combined Foreign Military Sales case and co-operative support arrangement that the UK has undertaken with the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force" title="United States Air Force">United States Air Force</a> since the Second World War. In RAF service, they will be known as the Airseeker.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup> Airseeker received its first operational deployment in August 2014, when it was deployed to the Middle East to fly missions over <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a> and <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a> as part of <a href="/wiki/Operation_Shader" title="Operation Shader">Operation Shader</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup></p>
<center>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Helicopters">Helicopters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Air_Force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Helicopters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Royal_Air_Force&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span> <small><i>(July 2017)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>An important part of the work of the RAF is to support the <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">British Army</a> by ferrying troops and equipment at the battlefield. However, RAF helicopters are also used in a variety of other roles, including support of RAF ground units and heavy-lift support for the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Marines" title="Royal Marines">Royal Marines</a>. The support helicopters are organised into the tri-service <a href="/wiki/Joint_Helicopter_Command" title="Joint Helicopter Command">Joint Helicopter Command</a> (JHC), along with helicopters of the <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">British Army</a> and <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a>. The only helicopters not coordinated by the JHC are those RN helicopters that are normally based on board a ship such as a destroyer or frigate, RAF Search &amp; Rescue, and training helicopter fleets.</p>
<p>The large twin-rotor <b><a href="/wiki/Boeing_Chinook_(UK_variants)" title="Boeing Chinook (UK variants)">Chinook</a></b>, based at <a href="/wiki/RAF_Odiham" title="RAF Odiham">RAF Odiham</a> provides heavy-lift support and is supported by the <b><a href="/wiki/Westland_Puma" class="mw-redirect" title="Westland Puma">Puma HC2</a></b> medium-lift helicopter based at <a href="/wiki/RAF_Benson" title="RAF Benson">RAF Benson</a>. The <b>Griffin HAR.2s</b> based at <a href="/wiki/RAF_Akrotiri" title="RAF Akrotiri">RAF Akrotiri</a> in the Cyprus <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_Base_Areas" class="mw-redirect" title="Sovereign Base Areas">Sovereign Base Areas</a>, the only remaining dedicated helicopter Search and Rescue force in the RAF. However, all UK military helicopter aircrew routinely train and practice the skills necessary for SAR, and the support helicopters based in the UK are available to the Government under <a href="/wiki/Military_Aid_to_the_Civil_Authorities" title="Military Aid to the Civil Authorities">Military Aid to the Civil Authorities</a> in case they are needed. The <b><a href="/wiki/Agusta_A109" class="mw-redirect" title="Agusta A109">A-109 Power Elite</a></b> aircraft of <a href="/wiki/No._32_Squadron_RAF" title="No. 32 Squadron RAF">32 (the Royal) Squadron</a> also provide VIP transport and military helicopter capabilities.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air_Mobility">Air Mobility</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Air_Force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Air Mobility">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/AirTanker_Services" title="AirTanker Services">AirTanker Services</a></div>
<p>The RAF operate the <b><a href="/wiki/C-17_Globemaster_III" class="mw-redirect" title="C-17 Globemaster III">Boeing C-17 Globemaster III</a></b> in the heavy strategic airlift role, originally leasing four from <a href="/wiki/Boeing" title="Boeing">Boeing</a>. These were purchased, followed by a fifth delivered on 7 April 2008 and a sixth delivered on 8 June 2008. The new aircraft entered frontline use within days rather than weeks. The MoD said there was "a stated departmental requirement for eight" C-17s and a seventh was subsequently ordered, to be delivered in December 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup> In February 2012 the purchase of an eighth C-17 was confirmed;<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[83]</a></sup> the aircraft arrived at RAF Brize Norton in May 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[84]</a></sup></p>
<p>More routine strategic airlift transport tasks are carried out by the <b><a href="/wiki/Airbus_A330_MRTT" title="Airbus A330 MRTT">Airbus A330 MRTT</a></b>, known as the Voyager in RAF service. The first Voyager arrived in the UK for testing at <a href="/wiki/MoD_Boscombe_Down" title="MoD Boscombe Down">MoD Boscombe Down</a> in April 2011,<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup> and entered service in April 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup> The Voyager received approval from the MoD on 16 May 2013 to begin air-to-air refuelling flights and made its first operational tanker flight on 20 May 2013 as part of a training sortie with Tornado GR4s. By 21 May 2013, the Voyager fleet had carried over 50,000 passengers and carried over 3,000 tons of cargo.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup> A total of 14 Voyagers are due to form the fleet, with 9 allocated to sole RAF use. As the Voyagers lack a refueling boom, the RAF has requested a memorandum of understanding (MoU) with the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force" title="United States Air Force">USAF</a> allowing the UK access to tankers equipped with refueling booms for its <a href="/wiki/Boeing_RC-135" title="Boeing RC-135">Boeing RC-135W Airseeker</a> <a href="/wiki/Signals_intelligence" title="Signals intelligence">SIGINT</a> aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p>Shorter range, tactical-airlift transport is provided by the <b><a href="/wiki/C-130_Hercules" class="mw-redirect" title="C-130 Hercules">Lockheed Martin C-130J Hercules</a></b>, known as Hercules C4 and C5 in RAF service and based at <a href="/wiki/RAF_Brize_Norton" title="RAF Brize Norton">RAF Brize Norton</a> in Oxfordshire. The draw-down of the Hercules C5 fleet has begun with the final aircraft planned to retire in 2019.The fourteen C4 extended variants are scheduled to retire on 31 March 2035. The <b><a href="/wiki/Airbus_A400M_Atlas" title="Airbus A400M Atlas">Airbus A400M Atlas</a></b> replaced the RAF's fleet of Hercules C1/C3 (C-130K) transport aircraft which were withdrawn from service on 31 December 2012 and will also replace the C4/C5 variants. Originally, 25 aircraft were ordered, although the total is now 22.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/No._32_Squadron_RAF" title="No. 32 Squadron RAF">No. 32 (The Royal) Squadron</a> replaced the Queen's Flight in 1995 and operate the <b><a href="/wiki/Agusta_A109" class="mw-redirect" title="Agusta A109">Agusta A109</a></b> and <b><a href="/wiki/BAe_146" class="mw-redirect" title="BAe 146">BAe 146 CC2</a></b> in the general air transport and VIP transport roles. The squadron is based at <a href="/wiki/RAF_Northolt" title="RAF Northolt">RAF Northolt</a> in west London. Aircraft operate with a priority for military needs over VIP transport. Two additional BAe 146s were purchased in March 2012 from <a href="/wiki/TNT_Airways" class="mw-redirect" title="TNT Airways">TNT Airways</a> and were refitted by <a href="/wiki/Hawker_Beechcraft" title="Hawker Beechcraft">Hawker Beechcraft</a> on behalf of <a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems" title="BAE Systems">BAE Systems</a> for tactical freight and personnel transport use.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup> The aircraft, designated as the BAe 146 C Mk 3, arrived in Afghanistan in April 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Training_aircraft">Training aircraft</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Air_Force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Training aircraft">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Elementary Flying Training, as well as Multi-Engine Lead-In training, is conducted on the <b><a href="/wiki/Grob_Tutor" class="mw-redirect" title="Grob Tutor">Tutor T1</a></b>. Basic fast jet training is provided on the <b><a href="/wiki/Short_Tucano" title="Short Tucano">Tucano T1</a></b> and initial helicopter training on the <b><a href="/wiki/Eurocopter_AS350" class="mw-redirect" title="Eurocopter AS350">Squirrel HT1</a></b>, at which stage aircrew gain their 'wings'. Multi-Engine aircrew, weapon systems officer (WSO) and weapon systems operator (WSOp) students are trained on the <b><a href="/wiki/Beechcraft_Super_King_Air" title="Beechcraft Super King Air">King Air</a></b> to gain their wings before a posting to an <a href="/wiki/Operational_Conversion_Unit" class="mw-redirect" title="Operational Conversion Unit">Operational Conversion Unit</a>. Advanced jet flying training is now provided on <b><a href="/wiki/BAE_Hawk" class="mw-redirect" title="BAE Hawk">Hawk T2</a></b> for fast jet aircrew and helicopter pilots complete a course on the <b><a href="/wiki/Bell_412" title="Bell 412">Griffin HT1</a></b>, before they are sent to their OCU, which trains them on a specific aircraft type in preparation for service with a front-line squadron. The OCUs use modified operational aircraft, such as the <a href="/wiki/Eurofighter_Typhoon_variants" title="Eurofighter Typhoon variants">Typhoon T3</a>, as well as sophisticated <a href="/wiki/Flight_simulator" title="Flight simulator">simulators</a> and ground training.</p>
<p>The <b><a href="/wiki/Grob_G_115" title="Grob G 115">Tutor</a></b> equips the fourteen <a href="/wiki/University_Air_Squadron" title="University Air Squadron">University Air Squadrons</a>, which provide University students an opportunity to undertake an RAF training syllabus based loosely on EFT to get them to and beyond solo standard. These units are co-located with <a href="/wiki/Air_Experience_Flight" title="Air Experience Flight">Air Experience Flights</a>, which share the same aircraft and facilities and provide air experience flying to the <a href="/wiki/Air_Training_Corps" title="Air Training Corps">Air Training Corps</a> and <a href="/wiki/Combined_Cadet_Force" title="Combined Cadet Force">CCF</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Volunteer_Gliding_Squadron" title="Volunteer Gliding Squadron">Volunteer Gliding Squadrons</a> also provide air experience flying to cadets using the <b><a href="/wiki/Grob_G_109" title="Grob G 109">Vigilant T1</a></b> motor-glider or the <b><a href="/wiki/Grob_G103a_Twin_II" title="Grob G103a Twin II">Viking TX1</a></b> conventional glider. Since April 2014, the Vigilant and Viking fleets have been grounded due to air-worthiness issues. As of March 2016, a 'recovery plan' is in place which will see Viking schools merged and expanded and significant reduction of the Vigilant fleet, which is to be retired by 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Future_aircraft">Future aircraft</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Air_Force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Future aircraft">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Future_of_the_Royal_Air_Force" title="Future of the Royal Air Force">Future of the Royal Air Force</a></div>
<p>The <b><a href="/wiki/F-35_Lightning_II" class="mw-redirect" title="F-35 Lightning II">F-35B Lightning II</a></b> is intended to enter service around 2020 under the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Combat_Aircraft" title="Joint Combat Aircraft">Joint Combat Aircraft</a> programme.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup> On 19 July 2012 the Defence Secretary, <a href="/wiki/Philip_Hammond" title="Philip Hammond">Philip Hammond</a>, in a speech in the USA, indicated that the UK would initially receive 48 F-35B to equip the Navy's carrier fleet and would announce at a later date what the final numbers would be. Jon Thompson, MOD <a href="/wiki/Permanent_Secretary" title="Permanent Secretary">Permanent Secretary</a>, told the House of Commons <a href="/wiki/Defence_Select_Committee" title="Defence Select Committee">Defence Select Committee</a>, in late 2012: "Our commitment over the first 10 years is for 48 F-35B". An order for the first 14 aircraft on top of the four already procured for operational test and evaluation is expected later in 2013. The first four of 14 production aircraft were ordered in November 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-14ordered_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14ordered-97">[96]</a></sup> Six further aircraft were ordered on 3 November 2015,<sup id="cite_ref-14ordered_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14ordered-97">[96]</a></sup> with expected delivery in 2016. In November 2015, the government commitment to order 48 F-35B aircraft by 2023,<sup id="cite_ref-BBC2015SDSR_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC2015SDSR-98">[97]</a></sup> 24 of which will be available for carrier duties.<sup id="cite_ref-SDSR2015_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDSR2015-99">[98]</a></sup> The 2015 Strategic Defence and Security Review stated the intent for the UK to purchase 138 F-35 aircraft over the life of the programme.<sup id="cite_ref-SDSR2015_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDSR2015-99">[98]</a></sup> The first F-35 aircraft arrived at RAF Fairford in Gloucestershire on 29 June 2016 after a Transatlantic crossing involving air to air refuelling.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/BAE_Taranis" class="mw-redirect" title="BAE Taranis">Project Taranis</a> is a technology demonstrator programme, possibly leading to a future Strategic <a href="/wiki/Unmanned_Combat_Aerial_Vehicle" class="mw-redirect" title="Unmanned Combat Aerial Vehicle">Unmanned Combat Aerial Vehicle</a> (UCAV) for both ground attack and reconnaissance roles.<sup id="cite_ref-Ministry_of_Defence_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ministry_of_Defence-101">[100]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/BAE_Mantis" class="mw-redirect" title="BAE Mantis">BAE Mantis</a> is another UCAV under development, with an autonomous capability, allowing it to fly itself through an entire mission. This is a potential candidate to fulfill a requirement for an <a href="/wiki/ISTAR" class="mw-redirect" title="ISTAR">ISTAR</a> UAV to enter service after 2015 as part of the RAF's Scavenger programme.<sup id="cite_ref-Mantis_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mantis-102">[101]</a></sup> On 5 October 2015, it was announced that the Scavenger programme had been replaced by <b>"Protector"</b>, a new requirement for at least 20 systems.<sup id="cite_ref-Protector_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Protector-103">[102]</a></sup> On 7 October 2015, it was revealed that Protector will be a derivative of the <a href="/wiki/MQ-9_Reaper" class="mw-redirect" title="MQ-9 Reaper">MQ-9 Reaper</a> with enhanced range and endurance.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[103]</a></sup></p>
<p>In July 2014 the House of Common Defence Select Committee released a report on the RAF future force structure that envisaged a mixture of unmanned and manned platforms, including a UCAV such as Taranis and further orders of F-35s, a service life extension for the Eurofighter (which would otherwise end its service in 2030) or a possible new manned aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[104]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Tutor, Tucano and King Air training aircraft are due to be replaced in the next few years through the implentation of the <a href="/wiki/UK_Military_Flying_Training_System" title="UK Military Flying Training System">UK Military Flying Training System</a>, a public-private partnership which has seen flying training for the Royal Air Force privatised and handed over to a civilian contractor, although military instructors remain. This will see the introduction of the <b><a href="/wiki/Grob_G_120TP" title="Grob G 120TP">Grob 'Prefect'</a></b>, the <b><a href="/wiki/Beechcraft_T-6_Texan_II" title="Beechcraft T-6 Texan II">Beechcraft T-6 Texan II</a></b> and the <b><a href="/wiki/Embraer_Phenom_100" title="Embraer Phenom 100">Embraer Phenom 100</a></b> into RAF service.</p>
<p>In November 2015, the Government confirmed in its <a href="/wiki/Strategic_Defence_and_Security_Review_2015" title="Strategic Defence and Security Review 2015">Strategic Defence and Security Review</a> that nine <b><a href="/wiki/Boeing_P-8_Poseidon" title="Boeing P-8 Poseidon">Boeing P-8 Poseidon</a></b> aircraft will be purchased for surveillance, anti-submarine and anti-surface ship warfare, filling a capability gap in maritime patrol that had been left since the cancellation of the <a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems_Nimrod_MRA4" title="BAE Systems Nimrod MRA4">Nimrod MRA4</a> programme in the 2010 SDSR.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[105]</a></sup> These aircraft were formally ordered on 11 July 2016 with the first expected to be delivered in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[106]</a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2016, it was announced that the RAF would see delivery of 29 <a href="/wiki/Eurocopter_EC135" title="Eurocopter EC135">Airbus H135</a> and 3 <a href="/wiki/Eurocopter_EC145" title="Eurocopter EC145">Airbus H145</a> helicopters for use as training aircraft. It was announced by Air Marshal Sean Reynolds, the Senior Responsible Owner for <a href="/wiki/UK_Military_Flying_Training_System" title="UK Military Flying Training System">UKMFTS</a>, that "Aircrew across the three Services will continue to conduct their basic and advanced rotary training at <a href="/wiki/RAF_Shawbury" title="RAF Shawbury">RAF Shawbury</a> and <a href="/wiki/AAC_Middle_Wallop" title="AAC Middle Wallop">Army Air Corps Middle Wallop</a>. Aircrew selected for training in mountain and maritime helicopter operations will receive instruction at <a href="/wiki/RAF_Valley" title="RAF Valley">RAF Valley</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Increase_of_fast_jet_squadrons">Increase of fast jet squadrons</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Air_Force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Increase of fast jet squadrons">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 20 September 2015, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sunday_Times" title="The Sunday Times">The Sunday Times</a></i> reported that the number of fast jet squadrons would increase due to threats posed by <a href="/wiki/Islamic_State_of_Iraq_and_the_Levant" title="Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant">Islamic State</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[108]</a></sup> This was later officially confirmed by the government in its <a href="/wiki/Strategic_Defence_and_Security_Review_2015" title="Strategic Defence and Security Review 2015">2015 Strategic Defence and Security Review (SDSR)</a> which outlined the government's commitment to 138 F-35 Lightning IIs and two additional Typhoon squadrons. On 4 December 2015, Chief of the Air Staff Air Chief Marshal Sir <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Pulford" title="Andrew Pulford">Andrew Pulford</a> announced his plans for one more combat squadron, in addition to the three outlined in the SDSR, to bring the total number of combat squadrons to ten.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[109]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span id="Symbols,_flags,_emblems_and_uniform"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Symbols.2C_flags.2C_emblems_and_uniform">Symbols, flags, emblems and uniform</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Air_Force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Symbols, flags, emblems and uniform">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Royal_Air_Force&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force_roundels" title="Royal Air Force roundels">Royal Air Force roundels</a> and <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force_uniform" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Air Force uniform">Royal Air Force uniform</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Air_Force_Ensign_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Air_Force_Ensign_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/220px-Air_Force_Ensign_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Air_Force_Ensign_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/330px-Air_Force_Ensign_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Air_Force_Ensign_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/440px-Air_Force_Ensign_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1440" data-file-height="720" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Air_Force_Ensign_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force_Ensign" title="Royal Air Force Ensign">Royal Air Force Ensign</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Royal_Banner_RAF.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Royal_Banner_RAF.svg/220px-Royal_Banner_RAF.svg.png" width="220" height="239" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Royal_Banner_RAF.svg/330px-Royal_Banner_RAF.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Royal_Banner_RAF.svg/440px-Royal_Banner_RAF.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="445" data-file-height="484" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Royal_Banner_RAF.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Colour" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen's Colour">Queen's Colour</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Following the tradition of the other British fighting services, the RAF has adopted symbols to represent it, use as rallying devices for members and promote <a href="/wiki/Esprit_de_corps" class="mw-redirect" title="Esprit de corps">esprit de corps</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force_Ensign" title="Royal Air Force Ensign">RAF Ensign</a> is flown from the flagstaff on every RAF station during daylight hours. The design was approved by <a href="/wiki/George_V" title="George V">King George V</a> in 1921, after much opposition from the <a href="/wiki/Admiralty" title="Admiralty">Admiralty</a>, who have the right to approve or veto any flag flown ashore or on board ship.</p>
<p>British aircraft in the early stages of the First World War carried the <a href="/wiki/Union_Flag" class="mw-redirect" title="Union Flag">Union Flag</a> as an identifying feature; however, this was easily confused with Germany's <a href="/wiki/Iron_Cross" title="Iron Cross">Iron Cross</a> motif. In October 1914, therefore, the French system of three concentric rings was adopted, with the colours reversed to a red disc surrounded by a white ring and an outer blue ring. The relative sizes of the rings have changed over the years and during World War II an outer yellow ring was added to the fuselage roundel. Aircraft serving in the Far East during World War II had the <a href="/wiki/File:RAF_Far_East_Command_roundel.svg" title="File:RAF Far East Command roundel.svg">red disc removed</a> to prevent <a href="/wiki/File:Japan_Air_Self-Defense_Force_roundel.svg" title="File:Japan Air Self-Defense Force roundel.svg">confusion</a> with Japanese aircraft. Since the 1970s, camouflaged aircraft carry low-visibility roundels, either red and blue on dark camouflage, or washed-out pink and light blue on light colours. Most uncamouflaged training and transport aircraft retain the traditional red-white-blue roundel.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> motto of the RAF, "<a href="/wiki/Per_ardua_ad_astra" title="Per ardua ad astra">Per Ardua ad Astra</a>", is usually translated as "Through Adversity to the Stars",<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-111">[110]</a></sup> but the RAF's official translation is "Through Struggle to the Stars".<sup id="cite_ref-RAF_.E2.80.93_Frequently_Asked_Questions_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RAF_.E2.80.93_Frequently_Asked_Questions-2">[1]</a></sup> The choice of motto is attributed to a junior officer named J S Yule, in response to a request from a commander of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Flying_Corps" title="Royal Flying Corps">RFC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Sykes" title="Frederick Sykes">Colonel Sykes</a>, for suggestions. The RAF inherited the motto from the RFC.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Badge_of_the_Royal_Air_Force" title="Badge of the Royal Air Force">Badge of the Royal Air Force</a> was first used in August 1918. In <a href="/wiki/Heraldry" title="Heraldry">heraldic</a> terms it is: "In front of a circle inscribed with the motto Per Ardua Ad Astra and ensigned by the Imperial Crown an eagle volant and affronte Head lowered and to the sinister".<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_111-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-111">[110]</a></sup> Although there have been debates among airmen over the years whether the bird was originally meant to be an albatross or an eagle, the consensus is that it was always an eagle.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[111]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2006 the RAF adopted a <a href="/wiki/Logotype" class="mw-redirect" title="Logotype">logotype</a> featuring a roundel and the Service's unabbreviated name (shown at the top of this article). The logotype is used on all correspondence and publicity material and aims to provide the Service with a single, universally recognisable brand identity.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ceremonial_functions_and_display">Ceremonial functions and display</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Air_Force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Ceremonial functions and display">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">

</td>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Red_Arrows">Red Arrows</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Air_Force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Red Arrows">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:RIAT_2016_F-35B_Typhoons_Red_Arrows.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/RIAT_2016_F-35B_Typhoons_Red_Arrows.jpg/220px-RIAT_2016_F-35B_Typhoons_Red_Arrows.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/RIAT_2016_F-35B_Typhoons_Red_Arrows.jpg/330px-RIAT_2016_F-35B_Typhoons_Red_Arrows.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/RIAT_2016_F-35B_Typhoons_Red_Arrows.jpg/440px-RIAT_2016_F-35B_Typhoons_Red_Arrows.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:RIAT_2016_F-35B_Typhoons_Red_Arrows.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Red Arrows in formation with an F35B and a pair of Typhoons at the <a href="/wiki/Royal_International_Air_Tattoo" title="Royal International Air Tattoo">Royal International Air Tattoo</a> in 2016.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Red_Arrows" title="Red Arrows">Red Arrows</a></div>
<p>The Red Arrows, officially known as the Royal Air Force Aerobatic Team, is the <a href="/wiki/Aerobatics" title="Aerobatics">aerobatics</a> display team of the Royal Air Force based at <a href="/wiki/RAF_Scampton" title="RAF Scampton">RAF Scampton</a>, with under-review plans to move to <a href="/wiki/RAF_Waddington" title="RAF Waddington">RAF Waddington</a>. The team was formed in late 1964 as an all-RAF team, replacing a number of unofficial teams that had been sponsored by RAF commands.</p>
<p>The Red Arrows badge shows the aircraft in their trademark <i>Diamond Nine</i> formation, with the motto <i>Éclat</i>, a French word meaning "brilliance" or "excellence".</p>
<p>Initially, they were equipped with seven <a href="/wiki/Folland_Gnat" title="Folland Gnat">Folland Gnat</a> trainers inherited from the RAF <a href="/wiki/Yellowjacks" title="Yellowjacks">Yellowjacks</a> display team. This aircraft was chosen because it was less expensive to operate than front-line <a href="/wiki/Fighter_aircraft" title="Fighter aircraft">fighters</a>. In their first season, they flew at 65 shows across Europe. In 1966, the team was increased to nine members, enabling them to develop their <i>Diamond Nine</i> formation. In late 1979, they switched to the <a href="/wiki/BAE_Hawk" class="mw-redirect" title="BAE Hawk">BAE Hawk</a> trainer. The Red Arrows have performed over 4,700 displays in 56 countries worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Royal_Air_Force_music">Royal Air Force music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Air_Force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Royal Air Force music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force_Music_Services" title="Royal Air Force Music Services">Royal Air Force Music Services</a></div>
<p>Headquarters Royal Air Force Music Services, located at <a href="/wiki/RAF_Northolt" title="RAF Northolt">RAF Northolt</a>, supports 177 professional musicians who attend events around the globe in support of the RAF. RAF Music Services were established in 1921, although the first RAF Director of Music was appointed in 1918. The Music Services were expanded for World War II and in the post war years there were ten established bands. Since then, Music Services has gradually been reduced in size and today comprises:</p>
<ul>
<li>Headquarters Music Services</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Central_Band_of_the_Royal_Air_Force" title="Central Band of the Royal Air Force">Central Band of the Royal Air Force</a> (including the RAF Salon Orchestra)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Band_of_the_Royal_Air_Force_College" title="Band of the Royal Air Force College">Band of the Royal Air Force College</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Band_of_the_Royal_Air_Force_Regiment" title="Band of the Royal Air Force Regiment">Band of the Royal Air Force Regiment</a></li>
<li>Band of the Royal Auxiliary Air Force<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Overseas_deployments">Overseas deployments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Royal_Air_Force&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Overseas deployments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<td><a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a></td>
<td>1940s–present</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/RAF_Gibraltar" title="RAF Gibraltar">RAF Gibraltar</a></td>
<td>No permanently stationed aircraft. RAF aircraft (e.g., Hercules transports) make regular visits.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a></td>
<td>1940–present</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/RAF_Akrotiri" title="RAF Akrotiri">RAF Akrotiri</a><br />
<a href="/wiki/RAF_Nicosia" title="RAF Nicosia">RAF Nicosia</a></td>
<td>During the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Crisis" title="Suez Crisis">Suez Crisis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Operation_Musketeer_(1956)" title="Operation Musketeer (1956)">Operation Musketeer</a> involved RAF aircraft based on Cyprus. Today, RAF aircraft are stationed at <a href="/wiki/RAF_Akrotiri" title="RAF Akrotiri">RAF Akrotiri</a> on Cyprus as part of <a href="/wiki/British_Forces_Cyprus" title="British Forces Cyprus">British Forces Cyprus</a>, from where, in 2014, aircraft were deployed in the <a href="/wiki/2014_military_intervention_against_the_Islamic_State_of_Iraq_and_the_Levant" class="mw-redirect" title="2014 military intervention against the Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant">intervention against ISIS</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr style="background:#efefef; color:black">
<td><a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a></td>
<td>2005–present</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/RAF_Al_Udeid" title="RAF Al Udeid">RAF Al Udeid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Udeid_Air_Base" title="Al Udeid Air Base">Al Udeid Air Base</a></td>
<td>Previously used in support of British operations in Iraq and Afghanistan (<a href="/wiki/Operation_Telic" title="Operation Telic">Op. Telic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Operation_Herrick" title="Operation Herrick">Op. Herrick</a> respectively), Al Udeid is currently in use as a Middle Eastern base for the RAF as well as being the headquarters for the RAF contribution against <a href="/wiki/Military_intervention_against_ISIL" title="Military intervention against ISIL">ISIL</a> on <a href="/wiki/Operation_Shader" title="Operation Shader">Op. Shader</a>. Currently an RAF <a href="/wiki/RC-135_Rivet_Joint" class="mw-redirect" title="RC-135 Rivet Joint">RC-135 Rivet Joint</a> aircraft is based there.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf" title="Persian Gulf">Persian Gulf</a></td>
<td>2001–present</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Operation_Veritas" title="Operation Veritas">Operation Veritas</a><br />
<a href="/wiki/Operation_Herrick" title="Operation Herrick">Operation Herrick</a>
<p><a href="/wiki/Operation_Toral" title="Operation Toral">Operation Toral</a></p>
</td>
<td>Chinooks provided airlift support to coalition forces. Additionally Merlin helicopters began tasking in late 2009 following the end of <a href="/wiki/Operation_Telic" title="Operation Telic">Operation Telic</a> (Iraq). Since late 2004 six <a href="/wiki/BAe_Harrier" class="mw-redirect" title="BAe Harrier">BAe Harriers</a> provided reconnaissance and close air support to the <a href="/wiki/International_Security_Assistance_Force" title="International Security Assistance Force">ISAF</a>. The Harriers were replaced by an equivalent force of <a href="/wiki/Panavia_Tornado" title="Panavia Tornado">Tornado GR4</a> in mid-2009. In August 2010, the Tornado force was uplifted to 10 aircraft. Other support units are deployed to <a href="/wiki/Muscat_International_Airport" title="Muscat International Airport">Muscat International Airport</a> in Oman, and air bases in the <a href="/wiki/UAE" class="mw-redirect" title="UAE">UAE</a> and the Kingdom of <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup> Combat operations within Helmand Province ended on 26 October 2014. The UK continues to contribute to NATO's Resolute Support mission with the RAF providing <a href="/wiki/A%C3%A9rospatiale_SA_330_Puma" title="Aérospatiale SA 330 Puma">Puma HC2</a>s<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[115]</a></sup> and other personnel within NATO formations.</td>
</tr>
<tr style="background:#efefef; color:black">
<td><a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a></td>
<td>1960s–present</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Bardufoss_Air_Station" title="Bardufoss Air Station">Bardufoss Air Station</a></td>
<td>RAF fighter and/or helicopter squadrons undergo winter-training here most years.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Ascension_Island" title="Ascension Island">Ascension Island</a></td>
<td>1982–present</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/RAF_Ascension_Island" title="RAF Ascension Island">RAF Ascension Island</a></td>
<td>Used as an air bridge between the UK and the <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">Falkland Islands</a>. <a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force" title="United States Air Force">United States Air Force</a> personnel are also stationed at this base.</td>
</tr>
<tr style="background:#efefef; color:black">
<td><a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">Falkland Islands</a></td>
<td>1982–present</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Port_Stanley_Airport" title="Port Stanley Airport">RAF Stanley</a><br />
<a href="/wiki/RAF_Mount_Pleasant" title="RAF Mount Pleasant">RAF Mount Pleasant</a></td>
<td>After initial use of the Airport at Stanley, the airbase/airport at Mount Pleasant was built to allow a fighter and transport facility on the islands, and to strengthen the defence capacity of BFFI (British Forces Falkland Islands). BFFI now replaced by BFSAI (<a href="/wiki/Military_of_the_Falkland_Islands" title="Military of the Falkland Islands">British Forces South Atlantic Islands</a>).</td>
</tr>
</table>

<td>1995–2007</td>
<td>Various helicopters</td>
<td>RAF enforced no-fly zones over the Balkans in the late 1990s and participated in the NATO interventions in Bosnia and Kosovo. RAF helicopters remained to provide support to the United Nations.</td>

<tr style="background:#efefef; color:black">
<td><a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a></td>
<td>2008–2012</td>

<td>Semi permanent detachment which involved helicopters giving support to the British Army</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a></td>
<td>2003–2011</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Operation_Telic" title="Operation Telic">Operation Telic</a><br />
Operation Kipion<br /></td>
<td>During the initial invasion, British strike fighters were used. Support aircraft such as the <a href="/wiki/Hercules_C130" class="mw-redirect" title="Hercules C130">Hercules C130</a>, <a href="/wiki/Puma_helicopter" class="mw-redirect" title="Puma helicopter">Puma helicopter</a> and <a href="/wiki/AgustaWestland_AW101" title="AgustaWestland AW101">Merlin helicopter</a> stayed in Iraq until the withdrawal in 2009. The Merlin helicopters were the last RAF aircraft to leave Iraq.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
<tr style="background:#efefef; color:black">
<td><a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a></td>
<td>1940–1979</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/RAF_Luqa" title="RAF Luqa">RAF Luqa</a></td>
<td>During the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Crisis" title="Suez Crisis">Suez Crisis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Operation_Musketeer_(1956)" title="Operation Musketeer (1956)">Operation Musketeer</a> involved RAF aircraft based on <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a></td>
<td>2011</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Operation_Ellamy" title="Operation Ellamy">Operation Ellamy</a></td>
<td>Enforcement of no fly zone in Libya according to <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_1973" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 1973">United Nations Security Council Resolution 1973</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
<tr style="background:#efefef; color:black">
<td><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a></td>
<td>2009–2013</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Creech_Air_Force_Base" title="Creech Air Force Base">Creech AFB</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nevada" title="Nevada">Nevada</a></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/No._39_Squadron_RAF" title="No. 39 Squadron RAF">No. 39 Squadron RAF</a> operated <a href="/wiki/MQ-9_Reaper" class="mw-redirect" title="MQ-9 Reaper">MQ-9 Reaper</a> <a href="/wiki/Unmanned_air_vehicle" class="mw-redirect" title="Unmanned air vehicle">UAVs</a> until moving to <a href="/wiki/RAF_Waddington" title="RAF Waddington">RAF Waddington</a> in the UK.</td>
</tr>
